_ngcontent-ng-c3190447963="" class="flex-column content-width brief-result-container"><!----><nde-record-title _ngcontent-ng-c3190447963="" data-qa="brief_result_title" class="record-title padding-right-big display-inline-block" _nghost-ng-c1259816950=""><h3 _ngcontent-ng-c1259816950="" class="visually-hidden ng-star-inserted"> Optimization of adaptive test design methods for the determination of steady-state data-driven models in terms of combustion engine calibration </h3><!----><h3 _ngcontent-ng-c1259816950="" ndetooltipifoverflow="" class="mat-body-large ng-star-inserted"><a _ngcontent-ng-c1259816950="" class="record-title anchor-tag-style" id="record_id_alma9933453768704146" data-qa="go_to_full_display" aria-label="Click to open the record's full display" href="/nde/fulldisplay?query=test+search&amp;tab=TAU&amp;search_scope=TAU&amp;searchInFulltext=true&amp;vid=972TAU_INST%3ANDE&amp;lang=en&amp;docid=alma9933453768704146&amp;adaptor=Local+Search+Engine&amp;context=L&amp;isFrbr=false&amp;isHighlightedRecord=false&amp;state="><nde-highlight _ngcontent-ng-c1259816950=""><span dir="auto" class="mat-body-medium ng-star-inserted">Optimization of adaptive <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">test</em></span> design methods for the determination of steady-state data-driven models in terms of combustion engine calibration</span><!----><!----></nde-highlight><!----></a></h3><!----><!----><!----><!----></nde-record-title><!----><div _ngcontent-ng-c3190447963="" class="flex-column record-details"><nde-record-main-details _ngcontent-ng-c3190447963="" _nghost-ng-c3864007556=""><div _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="record-main-details ng-star-inserted"><!----><div _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" data-qa="brief_result_creator" class="ng-star-inserted"><p _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="record-main-details-font-size"><span _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="light-text margin-right-small ng-star-inserted"> By </span><!----><nde-highlight _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556=""><span dir="auto" class="mat-body-medium ng-star-inserted">Sandmeier, Nino</span><!----><!----></nde-highlight><!----></p></div><!----><div _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" data-qa="brief_result_creationdate" class="ng-star-inserted"><p _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="record-main-details-font-size"><span _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="light-text margin-right-small ng-star-inserted"> Published on </span><!----><nde-highlight _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556=""><span dir="auto" class="mat-body-medium ng-star-inserted">2022</span><!----><!----></nde-highlight><!----></p></div><!----><!----><!----></div><!----></nde-record-main-details><!----><nde-record-summary _ngcontent-ng-c3190447963="" _nghost-ng-c1029101855="" class="ng-star-inserted"><div _ngcontent-ng-c1029101855="" class="flex-row ng-star-inserted"><span _ngcontent-ng-c1029101855=""><nde-paragraph-with-show-more-less-btn _ngcontent-ng-c1029101855="" showmorebtnlabel="nde.briefdisplay.summaryReadMore" showmorearialabel="nde.briefdisplay.summaryReadMore" showlessbtnlabel="nde.briefdisplay.summaryReadLess" showlessarialabel="nde.briefdisplay.summaryReadLess" _nghost-ng-c2657004550=""><div _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550="" class="flex-column flex-layout-start-start"><p _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550="" class="text-paragraph ng-star-inserted" style="-webkit-line-clamp: 2;"><nde-highlight _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550=""><span dir="auto" class="mat-body-medium ng-star-inserted">This thesis deals with the development of a model-based adaptive <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">test</em></span> design strategy with a focus on steady-state combustion engine calibration. The first research topic investigates the question how to handle limits in the input domain during an adaptive <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">test</em></span> design procedure. The second area of scope aims at identifying the <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">test</em></span> design method providing the best model quality improvement in terms of overall model prediction error. To consider restricted areas in the input domain, a convex hull-based solution involving a convex cone algorithm is developed, the outcome of which serves as a boundary model for a <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">test</em></span> point <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">search</em></span>. A solution is derived to enable the application of the boundary model to high-dimensional problems without calculating the exact convex hull and cones. Furthermore, different data-driven engine modeling methods are compared, resulting in the Gaussian process model as the most suitable one for a model-based calibration. To determine an appropriate <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">test</em></span> design method for a Gaussian process model application, two new strategies are developed and compared to state-of-the-art methods. A simulation-based study shows the most benefit applying a modified mutual information <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">test</em></span> design, followed by a newly developed relevance-based <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">test</em></span> design with less computational effort. The boundary model and the relevance-based <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">test</em></span> design are integrated into a multicriterial <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">test</em></span> design strategy that is tailored to match the requirements of combustion engine <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">test</em></span> bench measurements. A simulation-based study with seven and nine input parameters and four outputs each offered an average model quality improvement of 36 % and an average measured input area volume increase of 65 % compared to a non-adaptive space-filling <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">test</em></span> design. The multicriterial <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">test</em></span> design was applied to a <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">test</em></span> bench measurement with seven inputs for verification. Compared to a space-filling <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">test</em></span> design measurement, the improvement could be confirmed with an average model quality increase of 17 % over eight outputs and a 34 % larger measured input area.</span><!----><!----></nde-highlight><!----></p><!----><!----><button _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550="" color="primary" mat-button="" class="read-more basic-button mdc-button mat-mdc-button mat-primary mat-mdc-button-base ng-star-inserted" mat-ripple-loader-uninitialized="" combustion engine calibration)" mat-ripple-loader-disabled=""><span class="mat-mdc-button-persistent-ripple mdc-button__ripple"></span><span class="mdc-button__label"><span brief-result-container"><!----><nde-record-title _ngcontent-ng-c3190447963="" data-qa="brief_result_title" class="record-title padding-right-big display-inline-block" _nghost-ng-c1259816950=""><h3 _ngcontent-ng-c1259816950="" class="visually-hidden ng-star-inserted"> Using Hit Rate Tests to Test for Racial Bias in Law Enforcement: Vehicle Searches in Wichita  </h3><!----><h3 _ngcontent-ng-c1259816950="" ndetooltipifoverflow="" class="mat-body-large ng-star-inserted"><a _ngcontent-ng-c1259816950="" class="record-title anchor-tag-style" id="record_id_alma9933558149704146" data-qa="go_to_full_display" aria-label="Click to open the record's full display" href="/nde/fulldisplay?query=test+search&amp;tab=TAU&amp;search_scope=TAU&amp;searchInFulltext=true&amp;vid=972TAU_INST%3ANDE&amp;lang=en&amp;docid=alma9933558149704146&amp;adaptor=Local+Search+Engine&amp;context=L&amp;isFrbr=false&amp;isHighlightedRecord=false&amp;state="><nde-highlight _ngcontent-ng-c1259816950=""><span dir="auto" class="mat-body-medium ng-star-inserted">Using Hit Rate <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">Tests</em></span> to <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">Test</em></span> for Racial Bias in Law Enforcement: Vehicle <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">Searches</em></span> in Wichita </span><!----><!----></nde-highlight><!----></a></h3><!----><!----><!----><!----></nde-record-title><!----><div _ngcontent-ng-c3190447963="" class="flex-column record-details"><nde-record-main-details _ngcontent-ng-c3190447963="" _nghost-ng-c3864007556=""><div _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="record-main-details ng-star-inserted"><!----><div _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" data-qa="brief_result_creator" class="ng-star-inserted"><p _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="record-main-details-font-size"><span _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="light-text margin-right-small ng-star-inserted"> By </span><!----><nde-highlight _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556=""><span dir="auto" class="mat-body-medium ng-star-inserted">Persico, Nicola.; National Bureau of Economic Research.; Todd, Petra.</span><!----><!----></nde-highlight><!----></p></div><!----><div _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" data-qa="brief_result_creationdate" class="ng-star-inserted"><p _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="record-main-details-font-size"><span _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="light-text margin-right-small ng-star-inserted"> Published on </span><!----><nde-highlight _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556=""><span dir="auto" class="mat-body-medium ng-star-inserted">2004</span><!----><!----></nde-highlight><!----></p></div><!----><!----><!----></div><!----></nde-record-main-details><!----><nde-record-summary _ngcontent-ng-c3190447963="" _nghost-ng-c1029101855="" class="ng-star-inserted"><div _ngcontent-ng-c1029101855="" class="flex-row ng-star-inserted"><span _ngcontent-ng-c1029101855=""><nde-paragraph-with-show-more-less-btn _ngcontent-ng-c1029101855="" showmorebtnlabel="nde.briefdisplay.summaryReadMore" showmorearialabel="nde.briefdisplay.summaryReadMore" showlessbtnlabel="nde.briefdisplay.summaryReadLess" showlessarialabel="nde.briefdisplay.summaryReadLess" _nghost-ng-c2657004550=""><div _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550="" class="flex-column flex-layout-start-start"><p _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550="" class="text-paragraph ng-star-inserted" style="-webkit-line-clamp: 2;"><nde-highlight _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550=""><span dir="auto" class="mat-body-medium ng-star-inserted">This paper considers the use of outcomes-based tests for detecting racial bias in the context of police <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">searches</em></span> of motor vehicles. It shows that the <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">test</em></span> proposed in Knowles, Persico and Todd (2001) can also be applied in a more general environment where police officers are heterogenous in their tastes for discrimination and in their costs of <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">search</em></span> and motorists are heterogeneous in their benefits and costs from criminal behavior. We characterize the police and motorist decision problems in a game theoretic framework and establish properties of the equilibrium. We also extend the model to the case where drivers' characteristics are mutable in the sense that drivers can adapt some of their characteristics to reduce the probability of being monitored. After developing the theory that justifies the application of outcomes-based tests, we apply the tests to data on police <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">searches</em></span> of motor vehicles gathered by the Wichita Police deparment. The empirical findings are consistent with the notion that police in Wichita choose their <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">search</em></span> strategies to maximize successful <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">searches</em></span>, and not out of racial bias.</span><!----><!----></nde-highlight><!----></p><!----><!----><button _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550="" color="primary" mat-button="" class="read-more basic-button mdc-button mat-mdc-button Racial Bias in Law Enforcement: Vehicle Searches in Wichita )" mat-ripple-loader-disabled=""><span class="mat-mdc-button-persistent-ripple mdc-button__ripple"></span><span A <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">TEST</em></span> OF <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">SEARCH</em></span> AND BARGAINING THEORY</span><!----><!----></nde-highlight><!----></a></h3><!----><!----><!----><!----></nde-record-title><!----><div _ngcontent-ng-c3190447963="" class="flex-column record-details"><nde-record-main-details _ngcontent-ng-c3190447963="" _nghost-ng-c3864007556=""><div _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="record-main-details ng-star-inserted"><!----><div _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" data-qa="brief_result_creator" class="ng-star-inserted"><p _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="record-main-details-font-size"><span _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="light-text margin-right-small ng-star-inserted"> By </span><!----><nde-highlight _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556=""><span dir="auto" class="mat-body-medium ng-star-inserted">Beaudry, Paul ;  Green, David A. ;  Sand, Benjamin</span><!----><!----></nde-highlight><!----></p></div><!----><!----><div _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" data-qa="brief_result_ispartof" class="ng-star-inserted"><p _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="record-main-details-font-size"><span _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="light-text margin-right-small ng-star-inserted"> Part of </span><!----><nde-highlight _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556=""><span dir="auto" class="mat-body-medium ng-star-inserted">Econometrica, 2012-05, Vol.80 (3), p.1063-1104</span><!----><!----></nde-highlight><!----></p></div><!----><!----></div><!----></nde-record-main-details><!----><nde-record-summary _ngcontent-ng-c3190447963="" _nghost-ng-c1029101855="" class="ng-star-inserted"><div _ngcontent-ng-c1029101855="" class="flex-row ng-star-inserted"><span _ngcontent-ng-c1029101855=""><nde-paragraph-with-show-more-less-btn _ngcontent-ng-c1029101855="" showmorebtnlabel="nde.briefdisplay.summaryReadMore" showmorearialabel="nde.briefdisplay.summaryReadMore" showlessbtnlabel="nde.briefdisplay.summaryReadLess" showlessarialabel="nde.briefdisplay.summaryReadLess" _nghost-ng-c2657004550=""><div _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550="" class="flex-column flex-layout-start-start"><p _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550="" class="text-paragraph ng-star-inserted" style="-webkit-line-clamp: 2;"><nde-highlight _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550=""><span dir="auto" class="mat-body-medium ng-star-inserted">Does switching the composition of jobs between low-paying and high-paying industries have important effects on wages in other sectors? In this paper, we build on <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">search</em></span> and bargaining theory to clarify a key general equilibrium channel through which changes in industrial composition could have substantial effects on wages in all sectors. In this class of models, wage determination takes the form of a social interaction problem and we illustrate how the implied sectoral linkages can be empirically explored using U.S. Census data. We find that sector-level wages interact as implied by the model and that the predicted general equilibrium effects are present and substantial. We interpret our results as highlighting the relevance of <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">search</em></span> and bargaining theory for understanding the determination of wages, and we argue that the results provide support for the view that industrial composition is important for understanding wage outcomes.</span><!----><!----></nde-highlight><!----></p><!----><!----><button _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550="" color="primary" mat-button="" class="read-more basic-button mdc-button mat-mdc-button mat-primary mat-mdc-button-base ng-star-inserted" mat-ripple-loader-uninitialized="" mat-ripple-loader-class-name="mat-mdc-button-ripple" aria-label="Read More  (DOES INDUSTRIAL COMPOSITION MATTER FOR WAGES? A TEST OF SEARCH AND BARGAINING THEORY)" mat-ripple-loader-disabled=""><span class="mat-mdc-button-persistent-ripple mdc-button__ripple"></span><span class="mdc-button__label"><span _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550="">Read More</span></span><span class="mat-focus-indicator"></span><span class="mat-mdc-button-touch-target"></span></button><!----><!----></div></nde-paragraph-with-show-more-less-btn><!----></span></div><!----></nde-record-summary><!----><!----><!----><nde-record-snippet _ngcontent-ng-c3190447963="" data-qa="brief_result_snippet" _nghost-ng-c3527380962=""><div _ngcontent-ng-c3527380962="" class="border-for-snippet font-style-for-snippet snippet-container flex-row ng-star-inserted"><div _ngcontent-ng-c3527380962=""><mat-icon _ngcontent-ng-c3527380962="" role="img" class="mat-icon notranslate nde-mat-icon-size grey-icon-color mat-icon-no-color ng-star-inserted" aria-hidden="true" data-mat-icon-type="svg" data-mat-icon-name="quotation-marks"><svg width="100%" height="100%" viewBox="0 0 12 9" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" fit="" preserveAspectRatio="xMidYMid meet" focusable="false"><path d="M7.66675 8.75002H10.1667L11.1296 6.82432C11.5924 5.89862 11.8334 4.87787 11.8334 3.8429V2.91669C11.8334 1.53598 10.7141 0.416687 9.33341 0.416687C7.9527 0.416687 6.83341 1.53598 6.83341 2.91669C6.83341 4.2974 7.9527 5.41669 9.33341 5.41669M1.00008 8.75002H3.50008L4.46293 6.82432C4.92578 5.89862 5.16675 4.87787 5.16675 3.8429V2.91669C5.16675 1.53598 4.04746 0.416687 2.66675 0.416687C1.28604 0.416687 0.166748 1.53598 0.166748 2.91669C0.166748 4.2974 1.28604 5.41669 2.66675 5.41669L1.00008 8.75002Z" fill="#666666"></path></svg></mat-icon><!----></div><div _ngcontent-ng-c3527380962=""><nde-highlight _ngcontent-ng-c3527380962=""><span dir="auto" class="mat-body-medium ng-star-inserted">...? class="record-main-details-font-size"><span _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="light-text margin-right-small ng-star-inserted"> By </span><!----><nde-highlight _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556=""><span dir="auto" class="mat-body-medium ng-star-inserted">Cheung, Yeuk-Kwan E. ;  Vergados, J.D.</span><!----><!----></nde-highlight><!----></p></div><!----><!----><div _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" data-qa="brief_result_ispartof" class="ng-star-inserted"><p _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="record-main-details-font-size"><span _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="light-text margin-right-small ng-star-inserted"> Part of </span><!----><nde-highlight _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556=""><span dir="auto" class="mat-body-medium ng-star-inserted">Journal of cosmology and astroparticle physics, 2015-02, Vol.2015 (2), p.14-14, Article 014</span><!----><!----></nde-highlight><!----></p></div><!----><!----></div><!----></nde-record-main-details><!----><nde-record-summary _ngcontent-ng-c3190447963="" _nghost-ng-c1029101855="" class="ng-star-inserted"><div _ngcontent-ng-c1029101855="" class="flex-row ng-star-inserted"><span _ngcontent-ng-c1029101855=""><nde-paragraph-with-show-more-less-btn _ngcontent-ng-c1029101855="" showmorebtnlabel="nde.briefdisplay.summaryReadMore" showmorearialabel="nde.briefdisplay.summaryReadMore" showlessbtnlabel="nde.briefdisplay.summaryReadLess" showlessarialabel="nde.briefdisplay.summaryReadLess" _nghost-ng-c2657004550=""><div _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550="" class="flex-column flex-layout-start-start"><p _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550="" class="text-paragraph ng-star-inserted" style="-webkit-line-clamp: 2;"><nde-highlight _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550=""><span dir="auto" class="mat-body-medium ng-star-inserted">We consider the possibility of using dark matter particle's mass and its interaction cross section as a smoking gun signal of the existence of a Big Bounce at the early stage in the evolution of our currently observed universe. A study of dark matter production in the pre-bounce contraction and the post bounce expansion epochs of this universe reveals a new venue for achieving the observed relic abundance of our present universe. Specifically, it predicts a characteristic relation governing a dark matter mass and interaction cross section and a factor of 1/2 in thermally averaged cross section, as compared to the non-thermal production in standard cosmology, is needed for creating enough dark matter particle to satisfy the currently observed relic abundance because dark matter is being created during the pre-bounce contraction, in addition to the post-bounce expansion. As the production rate is lower than the Hubble expansion rate information of the bounce universe evolution is preserved. Therefore once the value of dark matter mass and interaction cross section are obtained by direct detection in laboratories, this alternative route becomes a signature prediction of the bounce universe scenario. This leads us to consider a scalar dark matter candidate, which if it is light, has important implications on dark matter <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">searches</em></span>.</span><!----><!----></nde-highlight><!----></p><!----><!----><button _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550="" color="primary" mat-button="" class="read-more _ngcontent-ng-c1259816950="" ndetooltipifoverflow="" class="mat-body-large ng-star-inserted"><a _ngcontent-ng-c1259816950="" class="record-title anchor-tag-style" test</em></span> detector</span><!----><!----></nde-highlight><!----></a></h3><!----><!----><!----><!----></nde-record-title><!----><div _ngcontent-ng-c3190447963="" class="flex-column _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" data-qa="brief_result_creator" class="ng-star-inserted"><p _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="record-main-details-font-size"><span _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="record-main-details-font-size"><span _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="light-text margin-right-small ng-star-inserted"> Part of </span><!----><nde-highlight _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556=""><span dir="auto" class="mat-body-medium ng-star-inserted">Nuclear instruments &amp; methods in physics research. Section A, Accelerators, spectrometers, detectors and associated equipment, 2015-03, Vol.777 (C), p.91-101</span><!----><!----></nde-highlight><!----></p></div><!----><!----></div><!----></nde-record-main-details><!----><nde-record-summary _ngcontent-ng-c3190447963="" _nghost-ng-c1029101855="" class="ng-star-inserted"><div _ngcontent-ng-c1029101855="" class="flex-row ng-star-inserted"><span _ngcontent-ng-c1029101855=""><nde-paragraph-with-show-more-less-btn _ngcontent-ng-c1029101855="" showmorebtnlabel="nde.briefdisplay.summaryReadMore" showmorearialabel="nde.briefdisplay.summaryReadMore" showlessbtnlabel="nde.briefdisplay.summaryReadLess" showlessarialabel="nde.briefdisplay.summaryReadLess" _nghost-ng-c2657004550=""><div _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550="" class="flex-column flex-layout-start-start"><p _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550="" class="text-paragraph ng-star-inserted" style="-webkit-line-clamp: 2;"><nde-highlight _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550=""><span dir="auto" class="mat-body-medium ng-star-inserted">The Heavy Photon <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">Search</em></span> (HPS), an experiment to <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">search</em></span> for a hidden sector photon in fixed target electroproduction, is preparing for installation at the Thomas Jefferson National Accelerator Facility (JLab) in the Fall of 2014. As the first stage of this project, the HPS <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">Test</em></span> Run apparatus was constructed and operated in 2012 to demonstrate the experiments technical feasibility and to confirm that the trigger rates and occupancies are as expected. This paper describes the HPS <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">Test</em></span> Run apparatus and readout electronics and its performance. In this setting, a heavy photon can be identified as a narrow peak in the e+e invariant mass spectrum above the trident background or as a narrow invariant mass peak with a decay vertex displaced from the production target, so charged particle tracking and vertexing are needed for its detection. In the HPS <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">Test</em></span> Run, charged particles are measured with a compact forward silicon microstrip tracker inside a dipole magnet. Electromagnetic showers are detected in a PbW04 crystal calorimeter situated behind the magnet, and are used to trigger the experiment and identify electrons and positrons. Both detectors are placed close to the beam line and split top-bottom. This arrangement provides sensitivity to low-mass heavy photons, allows clear passage of the unscattered beam, and avoids the spray of degraded electrons coming from the target. The discrimination between prompt and displaced e+e pairs requires the first layer of silicon sensors be placed only 10cm downstream of the target. The expected signal is small, and the trident background huge, so the experiment requires very large statistics. Accordingly, the HPS <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">Test</em></span> Run utilizes high-rate readout and data acquisition electronics and a fast trigger to exploit the essentially 100% duty cycle of the CEBAF accelerator at JLab.</span><!----><!----></nde-highlight><!----></p><!----><!----><button _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550="" color="primary" _ngcontent-ng-c1259816950="" class="visually-hidden ng-star-inserted"> Exploring the Interaction of Code Coverage and NonCoverage Objectives in SearchBased Test Generation </h3><!----><h3 _ngcontent-ng-c1259816950="" ndetooltipifoverflow="" class="mat-body-large ng-star-inserted"><a _ngcontent-ng-c1259816950="" class="record-title anchor-tag-style" id="record_id_cdi_swepub_primary_oai_research_chalmers_se_0c406db4_8f33_43a6_94a1_02d2b6094911" data-qa="go_to_full_display" aria-label="Click to open the record's full display" href="/nde/fulldisplay?query=test+search&amp;tab=TAU&amp;search_scope=TAU&amp;searchInFulltext=true&amp;vid=972TAU_INST%3ANDE&amp;lang=en&amp;docid=cdi_swepub_primary_oai_research_chalmers_se_0c406db4_8f33_43a6_94a1_02d2b6094911&amp;adaptor=Primo+Central&amp;context=PC&amp;isFrbr=true&amp;isHighlightedRecord=false&amp;state="><nde-highlight _ngcontent-ng-c1259816950=""><span dir="auto" class="mat-body-medium ng-star-inserted">Exploring the Interaction of Code Coverage and NonCoverage Objectives in SearchBased <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">Test</em></span> Generation</span><!----><!----></nde-highlight><!----></a></h3><!----><!----><!----><!----></nde-record-title><!----><div _ngcontent-ng-c3190447963="" class="flex-column record-details"><nde-record-main-details _ngcontent-ng-c3190447963="" _nghost-ng-c3864007556=""><div _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="record-main-details ng-star-inserted"><!----><div _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" data-qa="brief_result_creator" class="ng-star-inserted"><p _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="record-main-details-font-size"><span _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="light-text margin-right-small ng-star-inserted"> By </span><!----><nde-highlight _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556=""><span dir="auto" class="mat-body-medium ng-star-inserted">Fontes, Afonso ;  Gay, Gregory ;  Feldt, Robert</span><!----><!----></nde-highlight><!----></p></div><!----><!----><div _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" data-qa="brief_result_ispartof" class="ng-star-inserted"><p _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="record-main-details-font-size"><span _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="light-text margin-right-small ng-star-inserted"> Part of </span><!----><nde-highlight _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556=""><span dir="auto" class="mat-body-medium ng-star-inserted">Software testing, verification &amp; reliability, 2025-09, Vol.35 (6-7), p.n/a, Article e70009</span><!----><!----></nde-highlight><!----></p></div><!----><!----></div><!----></nde-record-main-details><!----><nde-record-summary _ngcontent-ng-c3190447963="" _nghost-ng-c1029101855="" class="ng-star-inserted"><div _ngcontent-ng-c1029101855="" class="flex-row ng-star-inserted"><span _ngcontent-ng-c1029101855=""><nde-paragraph-with-show-more-less-btn _ngcontent-ng-c1029101855="" showmorebtnlabel="nde.briefdisplay.summaryReadMore" showmorearialabel="nde.briefdisplay.summaryReadMore" showlessbtnlabel="nde.briefdisplay.summaryReadLess" showlessarialabel="nde.briefdisplay.summaryReadLess" _nghost-ng-c2657004550=""><div _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550="" class="flex-column flex-layout-start-start"><p _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550="" class="text-paragraph ng-star-inserted" style="-webkit-line-clamp: 2;"><nde-highlight _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550=""><span dir="auto" class="mat-body-medium ng-star-inserted">ABSTRACT
Searchbased <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">test</em></span> generation typically targets structural coverage of source code. Past research suggests that targeting coverage alone is insufficient to yield tests that achieve common testing goals (e.g., discovering situations where a classundertest throws exceptions) or detect faults. A suggested alternative is to perform multiobjective optimization targeting both coverage and additional objectives directly related to the goals of interest. However, it is not fully clear how coverage and goalbased objectives interact during the generation process and what effects this interaction will have on the generated <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">test</em></span> suites. In this study, we assess five hypotheses about multiobjective <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">test</em></span> generation and the relationships between coveragebased and goalbased objectives, focusing on the effects on coverage, goal attainment, fault detection, <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">test</em></span> suite size, <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">test</em></span> case length and the impact of the <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">search</em></span> budget. We generate <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">test</em></span> suites using the EvoSuite framework targeting Branch Coverage, three testing goalsException Count, Output Coverage and Execution Timeand combinations of coverage and goalbased objectives. Ultimately, we find that targeting multiple objectives does not reduce code coverage, yields no or minor reductions in goal attainment, butat the same timedetects more faults compared with singletarget configurations. In addition, it produces larger <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">test</em></span> suites, but <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">test</em></span> case length is not increased. The benefits of multiobjective optimization are often more limited than hypothesized in past research, but improved fault detection is still sufficient to recommend multiobjective optimization over targeting coverage or testing goals alone. Our study offers insights and guidance into how coverage and goalbased objectives interact during multiobjective <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">test</em></span> generation.
We assess five hypotheses about the interaction of structural coveragebased and tester goalbased objectives in searchbased <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">test</em></span> generation, focusing on coverage, goal attainment, fault detection, <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">test</em></span> suite size, <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">test</em></span> case length and the impact of <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">search</em></span> budget. Our study offers insights and guidance for future studies on multiobjective <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">test</em></span> generation.</span><!----><!----></nde-highlight><!----></p><!----><!----><button _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550="" color="primary" mat-button="" class="read-more basic-button mdc-button mat-mdc-button Coverage and NonCoverage Objectives in SearchBased Test Generation)" mat-ripple-loader-disabled=""><span class="mat-mdc-button-persistent-ripple mdc-button__ripple"></span><span class="mdc-button__label"><span _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550="">Read More</span></span><span class="mat-focus-indicator"></span><span _ngcontent-ng-c3190447963="" class="flex-column content-width brief-result-container"><!----><nde-record-title _ngcontent-ng-c3190447963="" data-qa="brief_result_title" class="record-title padding-right-big display-inline-block" _nghost-ng-c1259816950=""><h3 _ngcontent-ng-c1259816950="" class="visually-hidden ng-star-inserted"> A test for the search for life on extrasolar planets: Looking for the terrestrial vegetation signature in the Earthshine spectrum </h3><!----><h3 _ngcontent-ng-c1259816950="" ndetooltipifoverflow="" class="mat-body-large ng-star-inserted"><a _ngcontent-ng-c1259816950="" class="record-title anchor-tag-style" id="record_id_cdi_webofscience_primary_000177868700024" data-qa="go_to_full_display" aria-label="Click to open the record's full display" href="/nde/fulldisplay?query=test+search&amp;tab=TAU&amp;search_scope=TAU&amp;searchInFulltext=true&amp;vid=972TAU_INST%3ANDE&amp;lang=en&amp;docid=cdi_webofscience_primary_000177868700024&amp;adaptor=Primo+Central&amp;context=PC&amp;isFrbr=true&amp;isHighlightedRecord=false&amp;state="><nde-highlight _ngcontent-ng-c1259816950=""><span dir="auto" class="mat-body-medium ng-star-inserted">A <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">test</em></span> for the <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">search</em></span> for life on extrasolar planets: Looking for the terrestrial vegetation signature in the Earthshine spectrum</span><!----><!----></nde-highlight><!----></a></h3><!----><!----><!----><!----></nde-record-title><!----><div _ngcontent-ng-c3190447963="" class="flex-column record-details"><nde-record-main-details _ngcontent-ng-c3190447963="" _nghost-ng-c3864007556=""><div _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="record-main-details ng-star-inserted"><!----><div _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" data-qa="brief_result_creator" class="ng-star-inserted"><p _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="record-main-details-font-size"><span _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="light-text margin-right-small ng-star-inserted"> By </span><!----><nde-highlight _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556=""><span dir="auto" class="mat-body-medium ng-star-inserted">Arnold, L. ;  Gillet, S. ;  Lardire, O. ;  Riaud, P. ;  Schneider, J.</span><!----><!----></nde-highlight><!----></p></div><!----><!----><div _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" data-qa="brief_result_ispartof" class="ng-star-inserted"><p _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="record-main-details-font-size"><span _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="light-text margin-right-small ng-star-inserted"> Part of </span><!----><nde-highlight _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556=""><span dir="auto" class="mat-body-medium ng-star-inserted">Astronomy and astrophysics (Berlin), 2002-09, Vol.392 (1), p.231-237</span><!----><!----></nde-highlight><!----></p></div><!----><!----></div><!----></nde-record-main-details><!----><nde-record-summary _ngcontent-ng-c3190447963="" _nghost-ng-c1029101855="" class="ng-star-inserted"><div _ngcontent-ng-c1029101855="" class="flex-row ng-star-inserted"><span _ngcontent-ng-c1029101855=""><nde-paragraph-with-show-more-less-btn _ngcontent-ng-c1029101855="" showmorebtnlabel="nde.briefdisplay.summaryReadMore" showmorearialabel="nde.briefdisplay.summaryReadMore" showlessbtnlabel="nde.briefdisplay.summaryReadLess" showlessarialabel="nde.briefdisplay.summaryReadLess" _nghost-ng-c2657004550=""><div _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550="" class="flex-column flex-layout-start-start"><p _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550="" class="text-paragraph ng-star-inserted" style="-webkit-line-clamp: 2;"><nde-highlight _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550=""><span dir="auto" class="mat-body-medium ng-star-inserted">We report spectroscopic observations (400 800 nm, R approximate to 100) of Earthshine in June, July and October 2001 from which normalized Earth albedo spectra have been derived. The resulting spectra clearly show the blue colour of the Earth due to Rayleigh diffusion in its atmosphere. They also show the signatures of oxygen, ozone and water vapour. We tried to extract from these spectra the signature of Earth vegetation. A variable signal (4 to 10 +/- 3%) around 700 nm has been measured in the Earth albedo. It is interpreted as being due to the vegetation red edge, expected to be between 2 to 10% of the Earth albedo at 700 nm, depending on models. We discuss the primary goal of the present observations: their application to the detection of vegetation-like biosignatures on extrasolar planets.</span><!----><!----></nde-highlight><!----></p><!----><!----><button _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550="" color="primary" mat-button="" class="read-more basic-button mdc-button mat-mdc-button extrasolar planets: Looking for the terrestrial vegetation signature in the Earthshine spectrum)" mat-ripple-loader-disabled=""><span class="mat-mdc-button-persistent-ripple mdc-button__ripple"></span><span class="mdc-button__label"><span _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550="">Read More</span></span><span class="mat-focus-indicator"></span><span _ngcontent-ng-c1259816950="" class="visually-hidden ng-star-inserted"> Ex2: Monte Carlo Tree Searchbased test inputs prioritization for fuzzing deep neural networks </h3><!----><h3 _ngcontent-ng-c1259816950="" ndetooltipifoverflow="" class="mat-body-large ng-star-inserted"><a _ngcontent-ng-c1259816950="" class="record-title anchor-tag-style" id="record_id_cdi_proquest_journals_2759024344" data-qa="go_to_full_display" aria-label="Click to open the record's full display" href="/nde/fulldisplay?query=test+search&amp;tab=TAU&amp;search_scope=TAU&amp;searchInFulltext=true&amp;vid=972TAU_INST%3ANDE&amp;lang=en&amp;docid=cdi_proquest_journals_2759024344&amp;adaptor=Primo+Central&amp;context=PC&amp;isFrbr=true&amp;isHighlightedRecord=false&amp;state="><nde-highlight _ngcontent-ng-c1259816950=""><span dir="auto" class="mat-body-medium ng-star-inserted">Ex2: Monte Carlo Tree Searchbased <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">test</em></span> inputs prioritization for fuzzing deep neural networks</span><!----><!----></nde-highlight><!----></a></h3><!----><!----><!----><!----></nde-record-title><!----><div _ngcontent-ng-c3190447963="" class="flex-column record-details"><nde-record-main-details _ngcontent-ng-c3190447963="" _nghost-ng-c3864007556=""><div _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="record-main-details ng-star-inserted"><!----><div _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" data-qa="brief_result_creator" class="ng-star-inserted"><p _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="record-main-details-font-size"><span _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="light-text margin-right-small ng-star-inserted"> By </span><!----><nde-highlight _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556=""><span dir="auto" class="mat-body-medium ng-star-inserted">Ye, Aoshuang ;  Wang, Lina ;  Zhao, Lei ;  Ke, Jianpeng</span><!----><!----></nde-highlight><!----></p></div><!----><!----><div _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" data-qa="brief_result_ispartof" class="ng-star-inserted"><p _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="record-main-details-font-size"><span _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556="" class="light-text margin-right-small ng-star-inserted"> Part of </span><!----><nde-highlight _ngcontent-ng-c3864007556=""><span dir="auto" class="mat-body-medium ng-star-inserted">International journal of intelligent systems, 2022-12, Vol.37 (12), p.11966-11984</span><!----><!----></nde-highlight><!----></p></div><!----><!----></div><!----></nde-record-main-details><!----><nde-record-summary _ngcontent-ng-c3190447963="" _nghost-ng-c1029101855="" class="ng-star-inserted"><div _ngcontent-ng-c1029101855="" class="flex-row ng-star-inserted"><span _ngcontent-ng-c1029101855=""><nde-paragraph-with-show-more-less-btn _ngcontent-ng-c1029101855="" showmorebtnlabel="nde.briefdisplay.summaryReadMore" showmorearialabel="nde.briefdisplay.summaryReadMore" showlessbtnlabel="nde.briefdisplay.summaryReadLess" showlessarialabel="nde.briefdisplay.summaryReadLess" _nghost-ng-c2657004550=""><div _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550="" class="flex-column flex-layout-start-start"><p _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550="" class="text-paragraph ng-star-inserted" style="-webkit-line-clamp: 2;"><nde-highlight _ngcontent-ng-c2657004550=""><span dir="auto" class="mat-body-medium ng-star-inserted">Fuzzing is considered to be an essential approach to guarantee the reliability of deep neural networks (DNNs) based systems. The DNN fuzzing leverages various inputs prioritization methods to guide the testing process. The current research mainly focus on constructing testing metrics that symbolize the logical representation of the DNN to guide the generation of <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">test</em></span> cases, which neglects the potential performance brought by implementing heuristic algorithm. Moreover, the straightforward implementation of queue structure can not represent the metamorphic relationships between generated inputs in DNN fuzzing. Therefore, developing the appropriate heuristic algorithmbased inputs prioritization method is critical to improve the performance of DNN fuzzers. In this paper, we propose a Monte Carlo Tree <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">Search</em></span> (MCTS) based inputs prioritization method called E
x
2 $E{x}^{2}$ (Exploration and Exploitation) that formulates DNN testing exploration as the sequential decision process. The technique introduces an innovative treestructure design that schedules inputs from the statistical perspective. Different from traditional DNN testing, the batch pool is maintained in the form of nodes in MCTS. The links between nodes precisely represent the metamorphic relationship between input batches, which indicates the potential value for indepth <span class="text-bold-heavy ctm-highlight"><em class="font-style-normal">search</em></span>. Furthermore, a novel simulation mechanism is implemented to adapt MCTS in DNN testing, which attain better coverage feedback. The effectiveness of our method is comprehensively investigated on six popular deep learning models from LeNet and VGG families. The comparison experiments are conducted between DeepHunter, TensorFuzz, and DeepSmartFuzzer to demonstrate efficacy on various testing metrics. The experimental results show that the E
x
2 $E{x}^{2}$ significantly enhance the coverage gain of DNN fuzzing up to 30% against the best performance in comparison groups.</span><!----><!----></nde-highlight><!----></p><!----><!----><button
